</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="border-top:1px solid #aaa;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;">
<ul><li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg/16px-Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg/24px-Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg/32px-Aegopodium_podagraria1_ies.jpg 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Environment" title="Portal:Environment">Environment portal</a></li>
<li><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Earth_Day_Flag.png/16px-Earth_Day_Flag.png" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Earth_Day_Flag.png/32px-Earth_Day_Flag.png 2x" width="16"/> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Ecology" title="Portal:Ecology">Ecology portal</a></li></ul></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Pollution_sidebar" title="Template:Pollution sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Pollution_sidebar" title="Template talk:Pollution sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Pollution_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p><b>Pollution</b> is the introduction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contaminant" title="Contaminant">contaminants</a> into the natural environment that cause adverse change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Pollution can take the form of any substance (solid, liquid, or gas) or energy (such as radioactivity, heat, sound, or light). <a href="/wiki/Pollutant" title="Pollutant">Pollutants</a>, the components of pollution, can be either foreign substances/energies or naturally occurring contaminants. Although environmental pollution can be caused by natural events, the word pollution generally implies that the contaminants have an anthropogenic source – that is, a source created by human activities. Pollution is often classed as <a href="/wiki/Point_source_pollution" title="Point source pollution">point source</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nonpoint_source_pollution" title="Nonpoint source pollution">nonpoint source pollution</a>. In 2015, pollution killed nine million people worldwide (one in six deaths).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carrington_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carrington-3">[3]</a></sup> This remained unchanged in 2019, with little real <a href="/wiki/Progress" title="Progress">progress</a> against pollution being identifiable. <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">Air pollution</a> accounted for ¾ of these earlier deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1016/S2542-5196(22)00090-0_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-10.1016/S2542-5196(22)00090-0-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>Major forms of pollution include <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Litter" title="Litter">litter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">noise pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plastic_pollution" title="Plastic pollution">plastic pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soil_contamination" title="Soil contamination">soil contamination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_contamination" title="Radioactive contamination">radioactive contamination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermal_pollution" title="Thermal pollution">thermal pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visual_pollution" title="Visual pollution">visual pollution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">water pollution</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions_and_types">Definitions and types</span></h2><p>
Various definitions of pollution exist, which may or may not recognize certain types, such as <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">noise pollution</a> or <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>. The United States <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Administration" title="Environmental Protection Administration">Environmental Protection Administration</a> defines pollution as "Any substances in water, soil, or air that degrade the natural quality of the environment, offend the senses of sight, taste, or smell, or cause a health hazard. The usefulness of the natural resource is usually impaired by the presence of pollutants and contaminants."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In contrast, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> considers pollution to be the "presence of substances and heat in environmental media (air, water, land) whose nature, location, or quantity produces undesirable environmental effects."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow,_06.08.2010.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1453" data-file-width="1937" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow%2C_06.08.2010.JPG/220px-Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow%2C_06.08.2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow%2C_06.08.2010.JPG/330px-Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow%2C_06.08.2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow%2C_06.08.2010.JPG/440px-Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow%2C_06.08.2010.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smog_in_the_centre_of_Moscow,_06.08.2010.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">Smog</a> in the center of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow,_Russia" title="Moscow, Russia">Moscow, Russia</a> in August 2010</div></div></div>
<p>The major forms of pollution are listed below along with the particular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contaminants" title="Contaminants">contaminants</a> relevant to each of them:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">Air pollution</a>: the release of chemicals and <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">particulates</a> into the atmosphere. Common gaseous pollutants include <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chlorofluorocarbon" title="Chlorofluorocarbon">chlorofluorocarbons</a> (CFCs) and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a> produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_sector" title="Secondary sector">industry</a> and motor vehicles. Photochemical <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">smog</a> are created as nitrogen oxides and <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbons</a> react to sunlight. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" title="Atmospheric particulate matter">Particulate matter</a>, or fine dust is characterized by their <a href="/wiki/Micrometre" title="Micrometre">micrometre</a> size PM<sub>10</sub> to PM<sub>2.5</sub>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_pollution" title="Electromagnetic pollution">Electromagnetic pollution</a>: the overabundance of <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">electromagnetic radiation</a> in their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-ionizing" title="Non-ionizing">non-ionizing</a> form, such as radio and television transmissions, Wi-fi etc. Although there is no demonstrable effect on humans there can be interference with radio-astronomy and effects on safety systems of aircraft and cars.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">Light pollution</a>: includes light trespass, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Over-illumination" title="Over-illumination">over-illumination</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronomical" title="Astronomical">astronomical</a> interference.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Littering" title="Littering">Littering</a>: the criminal throwing of inappropriate man-made objects, unremoved, onto public and private properties.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">Noise pollution</a>: which encompasses <a href="/wiki/Roadway_noise" title="Roadway noise">roadway noise</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aircraft_noise" title="Aircraft noise">aircraft noise</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_noise" title="Industrial noise">industrial noise</a> as well as high-intensity <a href="/wiki/Sonar" title="Sonar">sonar</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Plastic_pollution" title="Plastic pollution">Plastic pollution</a>: involves the accumulation of plastic products and <a href="/wiki/Microplastics" title="Microplastics">microplastics</a> in the environment that adversely affects wildlife, wildlife habitat, or humans.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Soil_contamination" title="Soil contamination">Soil contamination</a> occurs when chemicals are released by spill or underground leakage. Among the most significant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_contaminant" title="Soil contaminant">soil contaminants</a> are <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">heavy metals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methyl_tert-butyl_ether" title="Methyl tert-butyl ether">MTBE</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herbicides" title="Herbicides">herbicides</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pesticides" title="Pesticides">pesticides</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chlorinated_hydrocarbons" title="Chlorinated hydrocarbons">chlorinated hydrocarbons</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Radioactive_contamination" title="Radioactive contamination">Radioactive contamination</a>, resulting from 20th century activities in <a href="/wiki/Atomic_physics" title="Atomic physics">atomic physics</a>, such as nuclear power generation and nuclear weapons research, manufacture and deployment. (See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpha_emitter" title="Alpha emitter">alpha emitters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Actinides_in_the_environment" title="Actinides in the environment">actinides in the environment</a>.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thermal_pollution" title="Thermal pollution">Thermal pollution</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> change in natural water bodies caused by human influence, such as use of water as coolant in a power plant.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Visual_pollution" title="Visual pollution">Visual pollution</a>, which can refer to the presence of overhead <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">power lines</a>, motorway <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_(advertising)" title="Billboard (advertising)">billboards</a>, scarred <a href="/wiki/Landform" title="Landform">landforms</a> (as from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strip_mining" title="Strip mining">strip mining</a>), open storage of trash, <a href="/wiki/Municipal_solid_waste" title="Municipal solid waste">municipal solid waste</a> or <a href="/wiki/Space_debris" title="Space debris">space debris</a>.</li>
<li><span class="anchor" id="Water_pollution"></span>Water pollution, caused by the discharge of industrial wastewater from commercial and industrial waste (intentionally or through spills) into surface waters; discharges of untreated sewage and chemical contaminants, such as chlorine, from treated sewage; and releases of waste and contaminants into surface runoff flowing to surface waters (including urban runoff and agricultural runoff, which may contain chemical fertilizers and pesticides, as well as human feces from open defecation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollutants">Pollutants</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pollutant" title="Pollutant">Pollutant</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canal-pollution.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Canal-pollution.jpg/200px-Canal-pollution.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Canal-pollution.jpg/300px-Canal-pollution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Canal-pollution.jpg/400px-Canal-pollution.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canal-pollution.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Lachine_Canal" title="Lachine Canal">Lachine Canal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, Canada</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yellow_Fish.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Yellow_Fish.jpg/200px-Yellow_Fish.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Yellow_Fish.jpg/300px-Yellow_Fish.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Yellow_Fish.jpg/400px-Yellow_Fish.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yellow_Fish.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Blue drain and yellow fish symbol used by the UK Environment Agency to raise awareness of the ecological impacts of contaminating surface drainage</div></div></div><p>A pollutant is a waste product that pollutes the environment, such as the air, water, or soil. A pollutant's severity is determined by three factors: its chemical type, concentration, extent of damage, and duration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_causes">Natural causes</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="133" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution's_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv" height="124" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv/220px--Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="702877" data-framerate="29.96999931427" data-height="288" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file, 512 × 288 (703 kbps)" data-width="512" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv" type='video/ogg; codecs="theora, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="184000" data-framerate="29.96999931427" data-height="120" data-shorttitle="VP9 120P" data-title="Lowest bandwidth VP9 (120P)" data-transcodekey="120p.vp9.webm" data-width="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/28/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv.120p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="256912" data-framerate="29.96999931427" data-height="180" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/28/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv.180p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="312616" data-framerate="29.96999931427" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="VP9 240P" data-title="Small VP9 (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="426" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/28/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv.240p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="317000" data-framerate="29.96999931427" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="426" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/2/28/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv/Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv.240p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ship_Tracks_Reveal_Pollution%27s_Effects_on_Clouds.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air pollution produced by ships may alter clouds, affecting global temperatures.</div></div></div>
<p>One of the most significant natural sources of pollution are <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcanoes</a>, which during eruptions release large quantities of harmful gases into the atmosphere. Volcanic gases include carbon dioxide, which can be fatal in large concentrations and contributes to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, hydrogen halides which can cause <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>, sulfur dioxides, which are harmful to animals and damage the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">ozone layer</a>, and hydrogen sulfides, which are capable of killing humans at concentrations of less than 1 part per thousand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Volcanic emissions also include fine and ultrafine particles which may contain toxic chemicals and substances such as <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">lead</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(element)" title="Mercury (element)">mercury</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">Wildfires</a>, which can be caused naturally by <a href="/wiki/Lightning_strike" title="Lightning strike">lightning strikes</a>, are also a significant source of air pollution. Wildfire smoke contains significant quantities of both carbon dioxide and carbon monoxide, which can cause <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suffocation" title="Suffocation">suffocation</a>. Large quantities of <a href="/wiki/Particulates" title="Particulates">fine particulates</a> are found within wildfire smoke as well, which pose a health risk to animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_generation">Human generation</span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle_emissions" title="Motor vehicle emissions">Motor vehicle emissions</a> are one of the leading causes of air pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_China" title="Air pollution in China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_the_United_States" title="Air pollution in the United States">United States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_Russia" title="Air pollution in Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_India" title="Air pollution in India">India</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_Mexico" title="Air pollution in Mexico">Mexico</a>, and Japan are the world leaders in air pollution emissions. Principal stationary pollution sources include <a href="/wiki/Chemical_plant" title="Chemical plant">chemical plants</a>, coal-fired <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_plants" title="Power plants">power plants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refineries</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aqueous_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aqueous-20">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Petrochemical" title="Petrochemical">petrochemical</a> plants, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_waste" title="Nuclear waste">nuclear waste</a> disposal activity, incinerators, large <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_meat_production" title="Environmental impact of meat production">livestock farms</a> (dairy cows, pigs, poultry, etc.), <a href="/wiki/Polyvinyl_chloride" title="Polyvinyl chloride">PVC</a> factories, metals production factories, plastics factories, and other <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a>. Agricultural air pollution comes from contemporary practices which include clear felling and burning of natural vegetation as well as spraying of pesticides and herbicides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>About 400 million metric tons of <a href="/wiki/Hazardous_waste" title="Hazardous waste">hazardous wastes</a> are generated each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The United States alone produces about 250 million metric tons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Americans constitute less than 5% of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_population" title="World's population">world's population</a>, but produce roughly 25% of the world's <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub></a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and generate approximately 30% of <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">world's waste</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In 2007, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> overtook the United States as the world's biggest producer of CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> while still far behind based on per capita pollution (ranked 78th among the world's nations).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG/220px-Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG/330px-Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG/440px-Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yangzhou_-_industrial_area_west_of_Wenfeng_Temple_-_P1130239.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An industrial area, with a power plant, south of <a href="/wiki/Yangzhou" title="Yangzhou">Yangzhou</a>'s downtown, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></div></div></div>
<p>Chlorinated hydrocarbons (CFH), heavy metals (such as chromium, cadmium – found in rechargeable batteries, and lead – found in lead paint, aviation fuel, and even in certain countries, gasoline), MTBE, zinc, arsenic, and benzene are some of the most frequent soil contaminants. A series of press reports published in 2001, culminating in the publication of the book Fateful Harvest, revealed a widespread practise of recycling industrial leftovers into fertilizer, resulting in metal poisoning of the soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Ordinary municipal <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a> are the source of many chemical substances entering the soil environment (and often groundwater), emanating from the wide variety of refuse accepted, especially substances illegally discarded there, or from pre-1970 landfills that may have been subject to little control in the U.S. or EU. There have also been some unusual releases of <a href="/wiki/Polychlorinated_dibenzodioxins" title="Polychlorinated dibenzodioxins">polychlorinated dibenzodioxins</a>, commonly called <i>dioxins</i> for simplicity, such as <a href="/wiki/2,3,7,8-Tetrachlorodibenzodioxin" title="2,3,7,8-Tetrachlorodibenzodioxin">TCDD</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>Pollution can also occur as a result of natural disasters. Hurricanes, for example, frequently result in sewage contamination and petrochemical spills from burst boats or automobiles. When coastal oil rigs or refineries are involved, larger-scale and environmental damage is not unusual. When accidents occur, some pollution sources, such as nuclear power stations or oil ships, can create extensive and potentially catastrophic emissions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>The motor vehicle is the most common cause of noise pollution, accounting for over 90% of all undesirable noise globally.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenhouse_gas_emissions">Greenhouse gas emissions</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">Greenhouse gas emissions</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="615" data-file-width="902" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png/300px-CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png/450px-CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png/600px-CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CO2-by-country--1990-2025.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Historical and projected CO<sub>2</sub> emissions by country (as of 2005).<br/> Source: Energy Information Administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">Carbon dioxide</a>, while vital for <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a>, is sometimes referred to as pollution, because raised levels of the gas in the atmosphere are affecting the Earth's climate. Disruption of the environment can also highlight the connection between areas of pollution that would normally be classified separately, such as those of water and air. Recent studies have investigated the potential for long-term rising levels of atmospheric carbon dioxide to cause slight but critical <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">increases in the acidity of ocean waters</a>, and the possible effects of this on marine ecosystems.
</p><p>In February 2007, a report by the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> (IPCC), representing the work of 2,500 scientists, economists, and policymakers from more than 120 countries, confirmed that humans have been the primary cause of global warming since 1950. Humans have ways to cut greenhouse gas emissions and avoid the consequences of global warming, a major climate report concluded. But to change the climate, the transition from fossil fuels like coal and oil needs to occur within decades, according to the final report this year from the UN's Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_health">Human health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soil_pollution#Health_effects" title="Soil pollution">Soil pollution § Health effects</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toxic_hotspots" title="Toxic hotspots">Toxic hotspots</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_pollution-related_diseases" title="List of pollution-related diseases">List of pollution-related diseases</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution#Health_effects" title="Air pollution">Air pollution § Health effects</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Health_effects_of_pollution.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2340" data-file-width="3294" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Health_effects_of_pollution.png/350px-Health_effects_of_pollution.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Health_effects_of_pollution.png/525px-Health_effects_of_pollution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Health_effects_of_pollution.png/700px-Health_effects_of_pollution.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Health_effects_of_pollution.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Overview of main health effects on humans from some common types of pollution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Adverse <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">air quality</a> can kill many organisms, including humans. Ozone pollution can cause <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_disease" title="Respiratory disease">respiratory disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Throat" title="Throat">throat</a> inflammation, chest pain, and <a href="/wiki/Nasal_congestion" title="Nasal congestion">congestion</a>. <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">Water pollution</a> causes approximately 14,000 deaths per day, mostly due to <a href="/wiki/Water_pollution" title="Water pollution">contamination of drinking water</a> by untreated <a href="/wiki/Sewage" title="Sewage">sewage</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>. An estimated 500 million <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indians</a> have no access to a proper toilet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Over ten million people in India fell ill with waterborne illnesses in 2013, and 1,535 people died, most of them children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> 
As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pollution&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, nearly 500 million Chinese lack access to safe drinking water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A 2010 analysis estimated that 1.2 million people died prematurely each year in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> because of air pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The high smog levels China has been facing for a long time can do damage to humans' bodies and cause different diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHO" title="WHO">WHO</a> estimated in 2007 that air pollution causes half a million deaths per year in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Studies have estimated that the number of people killed annually in the United States could be over 50,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Oil spills can cause <a href="/wiki/Human_skin" title="Human skin">skin</a> irritations and <a href="/wiki/Rash" title="Rash">rashes</a>. Noise pollution induces <a href="/wiki/Hearing_loss" title="Hearing loss">hearing loss</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_blood_pressure" title="High blood pressure">high blood pressure</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stress_(medicine)" title="Stress (medicine)">stress</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleep_disturbance" title="Sleep disturbance">sleep disturbance</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">Mercury</a> has been linked to <a href="/wiki/Developmental_disorder" title="Developmental disorder">developmental deficits</a> in children and <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">neurologic</a> symptoms. Older people are majorly exposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_effects_of_air_pollution" title="Health effects of air pollution">diseases induced by air pollution</a>. Those with heart or lung disorders are at additional risk. Children and infants are also at serious risk. <a href="/wiki/Lead_poisoning" title="Lead poisoning">Lead</a> and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toxic_metal" title="Toxic metal">heavy metals</a> have been shown to cause neurological problems. Chemical and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radioactive" title="Radioactive">radioactive</a> substances can <a href="/wiki/Carcinogen" title="Carcinogen">cause</a> <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mutagen" title="Mutagen">as well as</a> <a href="/wiki/Birth_defect" title="Birth defect">birth defects</a>.
</p><p>An October 2017 study by the Lancet Commission on Pollution and Health found that global pollution, specifically toxic air, water, soils and workplaces, kills nine million people annually, which is triple the number of deaths caused by AIDS, tuberculosis and malaria combined, and 15 times higher than deaths caused by wars and other forms of human violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The study concluded that "pollution is one of the great existential challenges of the <a href="/wiki/Anthropocene" title="Anthropocene">Anthropocene</a> era. Pollution endangers the stability of the Earth’s support systems and threatens the continuing survival of human societies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carrington_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carrington-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>A study published in 2022 in <i><a href="/wiki/American_Geophysical_Union#Publications" title="American Geophysical Union">GeoHealth</a></i> concluded that eliminating energy-related fossil fuel emissions in the United States would prevent 46,900–59,400 premature deaths each year and provide $537–$678 billion in benefits from avoided PM2.5-related illness and death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GeoHealth_20220516_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-GeoHealth_20220516-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2328" data-file-width="3660" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg/220px-Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg/330px-Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg/440px-Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pacific-garbage-patch-map_2010_noaamdp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Great_Pacific_garbage_patch" title="Great Pacific garbage patch">Great Pacific garbage patch</a></div></div></div>
<p>Pollution has been found to be present widely in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">environment</a>. There are a number of effects of this:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Biomagnification" title="Biomagnification">Biomagnification</a> describes situations where toxins (such as <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metals" title="Heavy metals">heavy metals</a>) may pass through <a href="/wiki/Trophic_level" title="Trophic level">trophic levels</a>, becoming exponentially more concentrated in the process.<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="540" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg/190px-CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg/285px-CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg/380px-CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg.png 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CO2_emission_pie_chart.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions" title="List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions">carbon dioxide emissions</a> by jurisdiction (as of 2015)</div></div></div></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">Carbon dioxide</a> emissions cause <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>, the ongoing decrease in the pH of the Earth's oceans as CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub> becomes dissolved.</li>
<li>The emission of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> leads to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> which affects ecosystems in many ways.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">Invasive species</a> can outcompete native species and reduce <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>. Invasive plants can contribute debris and biomolecules (<a href="/wiki/Allelopathy" title="Allelopathy">allelopathy</a>) that can alter soil and chemical compositions of an environment, often reducing native species <a href="/wiki/Competition_(biology)" title="Competition (biology)">competitiveness</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">Nitrogen oxides</a> are removed from the air by rain and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertiliser" title="Fertiliser">fertilise</a> land which can change the species composition of ecosystems.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smog" title="Smog">Smog</a> and haze can reduce the amount of sunlight received by plants to carry out <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">photosynthesis</a> and leads to the production of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropospheric_ozone" title="Tropospheric ozone">tropospheric ozone</a> which damages plants.</li>
<li>Soil can become infertile and unsuitable for plants. This will affect other <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Food_web" title="Food web">food web</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">Sulfur dioxide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a> can cause <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a> which lowers the <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a> value of soil.</li>
<li>Organic pollution of watercourses can deplete <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> levels and reduce species diversity.</li></ul>
<p>A 2022 study published in <i><a href="/wiki/Environmental_Science_%26_Technology" title="Environmental Science &amp; Technology">Environmental Science &amp; Technology</a></i> found that levels of anthropogenic chemical pollution have exceeded <a href="/wiki/Planetary_boundaries" title="Planetary boundaries">planetary boundaries</a> and now threaten entire ecosystems around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Toxicology and Environmental Health Information Program (TEHIP)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> at the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Library_of_Medicine" title="United States National Library of Medicine">United States National Library of Medicine</a> (NLM) maintains a comprehensive toxicology and environmental health web site that includes access to resources produced by TEHIP and by other government agencies and organizations. This web site includes links to databases, bibliographies, tutorials, and other scientific and consumer-oriented resources. TEHIP also is responsible for the Toxicology Data Network (TOXNET)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> an integrated system of toxicology and environmental health databases that are available free of charge on the web.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/TOXMAP" title="TOXMAP">TOXMAP</a> is a Geographic Information System (GIS) that is part of TOXNET. TOXMAP uses maps of the United States to help users visually explore data from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a>'s (EPA) <a href="/wiki/Toxics_Release_Inventory" title="Toxics Release Inventory">Toxics Release Inventory</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Superfund_Basic_Research_Program" title="Superfund Basic Research Program">Superfund Basic Research Programs</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h3>
<p>A 2021 study found that exposure to pollution causes an increase in violent crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_outcomes">School outcomes</span></h3>
<p>A 2019 paper linked pollution to adverse school outcomes for children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worker_productivity">Worker productivity</span></h3>
<p>A number of studies show that pollution has an adverse effect on the productivity of both indoor and outdoor workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation_and_monitoring">Regulation and monitoring</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regulation_and_monitoring_of_pollution" title="Regulation and monitoring of pollution">Regulation and monitoring of pollution</a></div>
<p>To protect the environment from the adverse effects of pollution, many nations worldwide have enacted legislation to regulate various types of pollution as well as to mitigate the adverse effects of pollution.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Control"><span class="anchor" id="Pollution_control"></span>Control</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Litter_trap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Litter_trap.jpg/220px-Litter_trap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Litter_trap.jpg/330px-Litter_trap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Litter_trap.jpg/440px-Litter_trap.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Litter_trap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A litter trap catches floating waste in the <a href="/wiki/Yarra_River" title="Yarra River">Yarra River</a>, east-central <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>, Australia</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="602" data-file-width="739" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg/220px-Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg/330px-Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg/440px-Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thermal-oxidizer-rto.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air pollution control system, known as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_oxidiser" title="Thermal oxidiser">thermal oxidizer</a>, decomposes hazard gases from industrial air streams at a factory in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="869" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg/220px-Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg/330px-Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg/440px-Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dust_collector_kosovo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Dust_collector" title="Dust collector">dust collector</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a></div></div></div><p>Pollution control is a term used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_management" title="Environmental management">environmental management</a>. It means the control of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emission_standard" title="Emission standard">emissions</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effluents" title="Effluents">effluents</a> into air, water or soil. Without pollution control, the <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">waste</a> products from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">overconsumption</a>, heating, agriculture, mining, manufacturing, transportation and other human activities, whether they accumulate or disperse, will degrade the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">environment</a>. In the hierarchy of controls, pollution prevention and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waste_minimization" title="Waste minimization">waste minimization</a> are more desirable than pollution control. In the field of <a href="/wiki/Land_development" title="Land development">land development</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low-impact_development_(Canada/US)" title="Low-impact development (Canada/US)">low impact development</a> is a similar technique for the prevention of <a href="/wiki/Urban_runoff" title="Urban runoff">urban runoff</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Policy" title="Policy">Policy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a> and monitoring/transparency/<a href="/wiki/Life-cycle_assessment" title="Life-cycle assessment">life-cycle assessment</a>-attached <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a> could be developed and enforced to control pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChangPires2015_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChangPires2015-58">[58]</a></sup> A review concluded that there is a lack of attention and action such as work on a <a href="/wiki/Global_governance" title="Global governance">globally</a> supported "formal <a href="/wiki/Applied_science" title="Applied science">science</a>–<a href="/wiki/Policy" title="Policy">policy</a> interface", e.g. to "<a href="/wiki/Group_decision-making" title="Group decision-making">inform</a> intervention, influence research, and guide funding".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10.1016/S2542-5196(22)00090-0_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-10.1016/S2542-5196(22)00090-0-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>
